"Atalopedes campestris","2007-07-20 13:35:34 -0400","At one point this female had 3 males buzzing around her.  I've seen very different courting styles among grass skippers.  The Zabulon male I witnessed courting was <a href=""http://www.flickr.com/photos/anitagould/274325009/"">patient</a>, even <a href=""http://www.flickr.com/photos/anitagould/274324112/"">tender</a>, following the female and touching her sometimes with his head or leg.  And Peck's seem to do likewise. Whereas these Sachems were all over the female, fluttering, jostling, trying to 'assume the position' with practically no preliminaries.  I saw another Sachem pair today, &amp; it was the same, so I suspect the behaviors may be species-specific.  But it might also have to do with other variables -- how alluring a given female is, whether it's early or late in the mating season, how many other males are around, etc.","New Jersey, United States",40.419728,-74.402155,"","Sachem","http://www.inaturalist.org/observations/513744","https://static.inaturalist.org/photos/654275/medium.jpg?1444428261","anita363",513744,"Sachem","Insecta",52075,"false",1,0,"2007-07-20 13:35:34","2007-07-20","2007-07-20 10:35:34 -0700","Eastern Time (US & Canada)",NA,"","","false","","",NA,3773,"2014-01-27 22:19:57 -0700","2017-04-23 20:51:09 -0700","research","CC-BY-NC-SA",NA,"false"
